          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=informative">informative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=living-vicariously">living-vicariously</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=conspiracy-theories">conspiracy-theories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=past-lives">past-lives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=glued-till-the-last-page">glued-till-the-last-page</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=romeos-and-juliets">romeos-and-juliets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195171430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3125438300868550696">I have always maintained the idea that Romeo and Juliet one of Shakespeare's immortalized tragedies were immortalized solely due to the fact the it is a tragedy. If Romeo and Juliet had a happy ending things would have been different and this immortalized classic would have joined the ranks of many "Happily ever after" stories and long forgotten. Don't get me wrong, "Happily ever after" stories are my favorite kind. There is something about those three lines at the end of the story that makes yo</span>
  <span id="freeText3125438300868550696" style="display:none">I have always maintained the idea that Romeo and Juliet one of Shakespeare's immortalized tragedies were immortalized solely due to the fact the it is a tragedy. If Romeo and Juliet had a happy ending things would have been different and this immortalized classic would have joined the ranks of many "Happily ever after" stories and long forgotten. Don't get me wrong, "Happily ever after" stories are my favorite kind. There is something about those three lines at the end of the story that makes you think of only the best possible future for the characters involved and makes you feel all happy and giddy inside. I am not a big fan of tragedies but William Shakesphere's "Romeo and Juliet" has a certain quality about it that makes you want to read it again and again. Knowing fully well that I am not going to get a happy ending and Romeo and Juliet are going to die in the end I can't help feeling or more correctly hoping that things would end differently each time I read. I keeping wishing that the messenger will reach Romeo in time or atleast he would wait a few more minutes until he drank the poison each and every time only to end in disappointment. But the uncanny thing is I wouldn't have it any other way. So when I first heard about this book I thought why not put my theory to test and conduct an experiment with this book which oddly enough drew its inspiration from this classic but has a chance of giving the whole story a different outcome. I will leave the discussion about the outcome there but one thing I have learned from this whole ordeal is it is not much about the outcome as the path that gets you there. When I started I was thinking of yet another love story with the heroine, namesake and descended of our late Bard's Juliet and her quest to find her Romeo and thus destined to play out a role the fates have inevitably cast on her. But what I got was so much more than that. It is not much of a love story as it is mystery. A mystery that involves secrets that are as old as 400 years. For one thing the book maintains that Shakespeare's "Romeo and Juliet" are based on actual characters and the story took place in Siena rather that Verona. According to this there are not two but three feuding families and the story has not ended with the death of the two young lovers but have been carried on for generations eventually falling on our fated protogonist Julie Jones or more precisely Guliette Tolomei. Embarking on a quest to retrieve a lost treasure on the wish of her dying aunt little did Julie know that she is unwillingly becoming a pawn in an age old conspiracy and family feud at the heart of Sienna. Perplexed at first as to why her late mother and aunt wanted her to learn about her ancestors she decides to go along for the ride for the sake of her mother's last wish. But soon she realizes the more deep she gets in to the mystery surrounding her ancestor the more danger she is getting her self into and the only person that can save her is her beloved Romeo. More than being an reinterpretation of "Romeo and Juliet" the book was more along the lines of Da Vinci Code. With clues waiting to be deciphered at every turn and conspiracies waiting to be unmasked this book read like a fast paced thriller with its base rooted in history. The extent of research put in to make this interesting story is highly commendable. I was surprised to find that the author herself was not of Italian origin as the writing style and the description of the places suggested, which itself is admirable. In this book Sienna itself is a character as the others and makes you feel like you actually took a trip to Italy. Any one who enjoys winding up with a good book should not let this one go. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3125438300868550696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109371876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109371876" />
    <a title="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1882027-elizabeth-of-silver-s-reviews"><img alt="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297997409p2/1882027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109371876?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/1882027-elizabeth-of-silver-s-reviews">Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109371876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11995715264926623755">Julie saw Umberto at the back of the room as she was leaving the stage. She knew this wasn't going to be good news because he wasn't smiling like always. "Aunt Rose has died" were the words that tumbled out of his mouth. As sad as Julie was, she also knew there would be something even more distressing....she had to face her twin sister Janice. Janice was four minutes younger than Julie, but she always upstaged her no matter what, and there was always conflict when Janice arrived on the scene.<br/><br/>It </span>
  <span id="freeText11995715264926623755" style="display:none">Julie saw Umberto at the back of the room as she was leaving the stage. She knew this wasn't going to be good news because he wasn't smiling like always. "Aunt Rose has died" were the words that tumbled out of his mouth. As sad as Julie was, she also knew there would be something even more distressing....she had to face her twin sister Janice. Janice was four minutes younger than Julie, but she always upstaged her no matter what, and there was always conflict when Janice arrived on the scene.<br /><br />It was pouring down rain the day they buried Aunt Rose. As soon as she was buried and they were leaving the gravesite, Janice demanded to see the will right then. The attorney did have the will and showed it to both girls, but nothing had been left to Julie...everything was left to Janice.<br /><br />Julie was devastated, but then Umberto said he had something that her mother had left for her....a key, a passport, and a letter. The letter wanted Julie to go to Italy, but Julie knew she couldn't go to Italy because she had been thrown out of the country when she was 18. Umberto had another means to get her to the country she was born in and to carry out her mother's wishes that Aunt Rose kept secret until she had passed away. Julie had no desire to go to Italy, but Umberto insisted...who couldn't resist a trip to Italy...mama mia :)<br /><br />Julie Jacobs aka as Giulietta Tolomei was on the plane to Italy the next day and met Eva Maria, an Italian citizen. She informed Giulietta that she knew her family and that her family and Giulietta's family were rivals back in the Middle Ages. Eva Marie took her under her wing and insisted that her grandson show Giulietta the town of Siena and keep her safe.<br /><br />The next day Giulietta went to the bank with her key. The bank manager had known Giulietta's father, and he took Giulietta to the safety deposit box with the matching key. What Giulietta found was her family and frightening and wonderful adventures. The key, the box her mother left her, and the story of Romeo and Juliet is the novel's main theme with lots of mystery and intrigue surrounding them. <br /> <br />Your interest won't wane especially if you look at Random House's website ( <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.randomhouse.com/rhpg/features/anne_fortier/photo-gallery.php">http://www.randomhouse.com/rhpg/featu...</a>) that corresponds with the book in pictures from the scenes of the book. I loved it as the mysteries unraveled.<br /><br />This book is outstanding...the storyline, the descriptions, the characters, and Italy. <br /><br />I loved how the book went back and forth from the 1300's to present day using the story of Romeo and Juliet as the main plot and how the main characters unraveled family and life-long mysteries....you will love the present-day characters Julie and Janice Jacobs also known as Giulietta and Giannozza Talomei.<br /><br />I couldn't put it down. I loved "being in Italy" again, and could just see the buildings and all the quaintness of the country and the city of Siena. The web page Random House set up for the book adds to your interest because the pictures go along with the pages of the book. <br /><br />I can't see how it wouldn't be liked...it is a book you won't want to miss. It has something for everyone...history, romance, mystery, betrayal, life in the 1300's in Italy, ancestors, middle-age family feuds, suspense, and a great author. Ms. Fortier did a superb job with her novel.<br /><br />It is absolutely wonderful right up to the last page. You will not want it to end. What an extraordinary novel. ENJOY!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11995715264926623755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_164032384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164032384" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4075354-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606221712p2/4075354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164032384?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4075354-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=abc-challenges">abc-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=tbr-pile-challenges">tbr-pile-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=ladies-and-lit-bookclub">ladies-and-lit-bookclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164032384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17461801312409897444">I admit, I’m kind of waffling between 3 and 4 stars with this one. I thought I would love this book, and at the story’s beginning, I did. I was really pulled in by the mystery – why did great-aunt Rose leave Julie only a key to a safe deposit box in Italy, while leaving Julie’s twin Janice everything else? Why did she keep their identities a secret and only divulge their real names and circumstances of their early life in Siena, Italy upon her death?<br/><br/>The further I read, the less compelled I becam</span>
  <span id="freeText17461801312409897444" style="display:none">I admit, I’m kind of waffling between 3 and 4 stars with this one. I thought I would love this book, and at the story’s beginning, I did. I was really pulled in by the mystery – why did great-aunt Rose leave Julie only a key to a safe deposit box in Italy, while leaving Julie’s twin Janice everything else? Why did she keep their identities a secret and only divulge their real names and circumstances of their early life in Siena, Italy upon her death?<br /><br />The further I read, the less compelled I became. The mystery was still good, but the characters were not as compelling as I’d hoped, nor were their interactions with one another always realistic.<br /><br />The historical story of Romeo and Juliet were most interesting to me, though at times they were a little overly dramatic. I also thought she would go into more depth with their love story, but it was pretty much “insta-love,” which may have been the point, but just isn’t my favorite type of storyline. I did love the danger of the Palo, the prestigious horse race between prominent families in Siena, as well as the danger in Romeo challenging the most powerful man in Siena all for his love of Juliet. The characters were often dramatic, but it fit that period and felt right in the story.<br /><br />The drama between Julie and Janice in the modern day was something I could have done without. Julie’s constant inner monologues about what Janice would say or do got a bit old, as did their bickering later on in the story. They came across as teenagers instead of twenty-five year olds, and I guess their bickering was supposed to be humorous, but to me it was just tiring. It just seemed to take up too much of the story.<br /><br />The relationship that developed between Julie and Alessandro, which up until a certain point contained great chemistry, didn’t always ring true. I couldn’t believe how naive Julie was about the whole thing. She basically set herself up for being hurt, and it just wasn’t a realistic decision for her to make. Up until her sister showed up, Julie was level-headed, but after that point, she changed.<br /><br />The last 100 or so pages were really exciting, though I found the Italian gangsters to be cheesy &amp; unrealistic and Janice's antics to be over-the-top. Overall, I suppose for me the book lost it’s serious, realistic tone. Although it’s a work of fiction, it held such weight in the beginning, but sadly that weighty factor didn’t carry on throughout the rest of the story. There were twists and the mystery was finally unraveled. It all just ended up being fluffier than what I thought I was getting into at the story’s beginning and what I wanted out of it. <br /><br />I would definitely be interested in reading more of Fortier’s books in the future – her upcoming title, The Lost Sisterhood, is on my to-read list.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17461801312409897444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120781281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120781281" />
    <a title="Tonya Leavitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/960172-tonya-leavitt"><img alt="Tonya Leavitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229211658p2/960172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120781281?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tonya Leavitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tonya Leavitt" href="/user/show/960172-tonya-leavitt">Tonya Leavitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/960172-tonya-leavitt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120781281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15002890956668786425">Modern day Juliet finds her own Romeo while searching for the real Romeo and Juliet, who inspired Shakespeare's famous play. Basically you get two love stories for the price of one, told side by side and all wrapped up in history, mystery, family drama, tragedy, and sprinkled with Shakespeare. If I was on a hamster wheel with my last two reads (Fallen and Torment) then I was on a bullet train with this book and I had a fabulous trip! <br/><br/>Just can't complain about....Siena, Italy, the setting of this</span>
  <span id="freeText15002890956668786425" style="display:none">Modern day Juliet finds her own Romeo while searching for the real Romeo and Juliet, who inspired Shakespeare's famous play. Basically you get two love stories for the price of one, told side by side and all wrapped up in history, mystery, family drama, tragedy, and sprinkled with Shakespeare. If I was on a hamster wheel with my last two reads (Fallen and Torment) then I was on a bullet train with this book and I had a fabulous trip! <br /><br />Just can't complain about....Siena, Italy, the setting of this book sounds so beautiful and rich with history and culture. I'd love to visit someday. Janice, Julie's polar opposite twin sister - now she's a character! Some of my favorite lines in the book come from Janice, especially when she talks about driving the bus into cherry town, I laughed out loud. Alessandro, dreamy Italian guy, small Euro swimsuit :) Clever and beautifully crafted literacy that just feels good coming off your tongue.<br /><br />Just a few complaints though....This author knows how to tell a great story but I think she failed when it came to developing her main character, Julie Jacobs (aka Giulietta or Juliet). It wasn't until after I finished the book that I realized I didn't know what Julie looked like; I couldn't picture her in my mind. I didn't even really like her very much and couldn't see why any guy, especially Romeo, would like her either. Some authors describe their characters so well that you feel like they become a familiar old friend. It doesn't help that Julie does everything opposite of what she should do. She trusts all the wrong people; when someone tells her the truth she thinks they are lying, when someone is lying she completely falls for it. She runs when she should stay put and she lingers too long when she should really being trying to get away. All of this makes it really hard to believe that Romeo is actually going to fall in love with her after a week or two. I enjoyed the mid-evil Romeo and Juliet story more that the modern-day one. However, it is a pretty romantic idea that you could go to Italy and find a gorgeous Italian guy to fall in love with you. That's why I read books - for the fairytale - not for reality. The author did such a great job at including parts of Shakespeare's Romeo and Juliet. The whole time I was waiting for a balcony scene and it never came - slightly disappointed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15002890956668786425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113939621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113939621" />
    <a title="Camilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4072455-camilla"><img alt="Camilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554065817p2/4072455.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113939621?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camilla" href="/user/show/4072455-camilla">Camilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788702077322" href="/book/show/11620780-julie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4072455-camilla?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4072455-camilla?shelf=dansk-danish">dansk-danish</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113939621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5887174069296798700">Its been a while since I've read a book, where there's no biting during sex, or just no sex at all.. And its been a while since I've read a book, where there's not one single guy-on-guy make out scene.. (Yeah, dont ask ;) And its been even longer since I've read a book in Danish.. and I kinda wish I hadnt actually.. I didnt like the translation -at all- which is very strange considering that the author is from Denmark. I cant believe she approved this version, but whatever.. The translator was p</span>
  <span id="freeText5887174069296798700" style="display:none">Its been a while since I've read a book, where there's no biting during sex, or just no sex at all.. And its been a while since I've read a book, where there's not one single guy-on-guy make out scene.. (Yeah, dont ask ;) And its been even longer since I've read a book in Danish.. and I kinda wish I hadnt actually.. I didnt like the translation -at all- which is very strange considering that the author is from Denmark. I cant believe she approved this version, but whatever.. The translator was probably drunk when she/he did this.. ( We like being drunk in Denmark FYI ;)<br /><br />Not counting the translation, I really enjoyed this book. I thought the plot was great, and it definitely had me turning the page in wonder, and I couldnt wait to find out what happened next.<br /><br />The book is 523 pages long, and I was reading the last 100 pages up until page number 500 on a train, and I'm pretty sure everyone could see from my facial expressions just how exciting the book was getting. Me biting my nails, shaking my head, when there was a new twist (and there were a lot) and I caught myself laughing out loud a couple of times.. (Yes, very embarrassing BTW) Mostly on the expense of Janice though..<br /><br />We're reading this from Julie's (her name is Julie, in the Danish version) POV, and I really dont like 1st person POV's, but I think it worked out fine in this book. <br /><br />I dont know if it was just because I missed something, or its because of the 1st person POV, but even after finishing this book, I cant tell you what Julie looked like. I thought she was kinda 'blah' and she was never mentioned as being as beautiful as the first 'Juliet' but that probably doesnt matter though.. This book is about love, and the story of Romeo and Juliet (Or Julie as it is in Denmark)<br /><br />I wanted Julie and Romeo to end up together, from the first time they met, when they didnt like each other at all, and I got my wish! So for that, and for making me look like an idiot on the train, this book definitely deserves 4 stars!<br /><br />If it hadnt been for a translator on drugs, it could probably be a 5 star book... </span>
  <a data-text-id="5887174069296798700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And after three days of not being able to get it out of my mind, I knew I would have to purchase this book.<br/><br/>I am not a huge Shakespeare fan, Yes I am aware of the classic's basic story line (thanks to high school English) but that is really all I ever got into.   <span id="freeText179144153814309613" style="display:none">I read alot of books, but rarely do I go out and purchase them. I had to wait a few days to decide what to rate this book. I knew I liked it ALOT, but I had to really think is it one that I would be comfortable to have on my book shelf. And after three days of not being able to get it out of my mind, I knew I would have to purchase this book.<br /><br />I am not a huge Shakespeare fan, Yes I am aware of the classic's basic story line (thanks to high school English) but that is really all I ever got into. So picking up this book I really really hoped it wasn't going to be a tragedy like the play. I enjoy happy endings. The story starts with Julie finding she is not who she thought she was, but was actually Guilletta from Senia Italy, and was related to the real Guilletta from the play. Except there is a hidden treasure that revolves around Romeo and Juliet's story. And that treasure and curse is tied to there family. As she uncovers the mystery, she is chased, followed, falls in love and needs to find her modern day Romeo to save her. <br /><br />Read it you will not be disappointed. And after Christmas you can borrow mine... drat being on a budget!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10474559800545459409">Just received my advanced copy. Can't wait to start.<br/><br/><br/> The novel goes back and forth between a modern day love story and the original story about Romeo and Juliet which takes place in 1340 in Sienna. According to the book Shakespeare based his story of Romeo and Juliet on real people and changed the details and the setting from Sienna to Verona. <br/> Juliet, who is the main character of the book, inherits a key to a safety deposit box in Sienna, Italy. She travels there to find her treasure and discov</span>
  <span id="freeText10474559800545459409" style="display:none">Just received my advanced copy. Can't wait to start.<br /><br /><br /> The novel goes back and forth between a modern day love story and the original story about Romeo and Juliet which takes place in 1340 in Sienna. According to the book Shakespeare based his story of Romeo and Juliet on real people and changed the details and the setting from Sienna to Verona. <br /> Juliet, who is the main character of the book, inherits a key to a safety deposit box in Sienna, Italy. She travels there to find her treasure and discovers that she is a direct descendant of Juliet and also finds out that the notorious curse that was put upon both of the star crossed lovers houses still exists. The only way for her to end the curse is to find her modern day Romeo. <br /> The story line is very clever and if you enjoy the story of Romeo and Juliet you will like this version of the popular tale. There are a lot of twists and turns which keeps you guessing along the way. And it's fun to read the original romantic story as you are reading the contemporary version.<br /> </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasminka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasminka" href="/user/show/4495283-jasminka">Jasminka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4495283-jasminka?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201316006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4980597640531060224">"Juliet" is a story of everlasting and immortal love of Romeo and Juliette, but not as in Shakespeare’s tale. This is a a story within a story novel, the narrative switches between present day and the middle ages in 1340. Romance( in great amounts), mystery, history, treasure hunts, curses, suspense, adventure - all set in glorious Italy, in Siena (not Verona!).There are so many deceptive twists and turns in this entertaining novel, it's definitely a page-turner, and that is the reason why I gav</span>
  <span id="freeText4980597640531060224" style="display:none">"Juliet" is a story of everlasting and immortal love of Romeo and Juliette, but not as in Shakespeare’s tale. This is a a story within a story novel, the narrative switches between present day and the middle ages in 1340. Romance( in great amounts), mystery, history, treasure hunts, curses, suspense, adventure - all set in glorious Italy, in Siena (not Verona!).There are so many deceptive twists and turns in this entertaining novel, it's definitely a page-turner, and that is the reason why I gave it 4 stars instead of 3(too many stereotypical and naive characters, unbelievable events in present day, strange "reincarnation" – thing, too many "coincidences", several characters with the same names, bizarre happenings at the ending …). But, the history of medieval Siena, interesting premise, entertaining, imaginative storyline, the way chapters alternating between past and present... all that and more - so enchanting! Once I've started, I couldn't put it down!!!! Maybe it is not really a great literature, but I liked this beautiful, refreshing and enjoyable story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4980597640531060224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127996457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14420852697269016434">What a mess of a book! I picked it up because I love the story and it even started well. A few pages in, I was disappointed. Fortier has a poor grasp of dialogue, especially medieval, and I soon found myself laughing at her serious conversations. The plot became ridiculous about half way through and by the end it was positively creaky with the scene in the sewers serving no purpose, except perhaps as a rather weak foreshadowing of what is to come. The relationship between the sisters veers all o</span>
  <span id="freeText14420852697269016434" style="display:none">What a mess of a book! I picked it up because I love the story and it even started well. A few pages in, I was disappointed. Fortier has a poor grasp of dialogue, especially medieval, and I soon found myself laughing at her serious conversations. The plot became ridiculous about half way through and by the end it was positively creaky with the scene in the sewers serving no purpose, except perhaps as a rather weak foreshadowing of what is to come. The relationship between the sisters veers all over the place and the love interest is plain silly.<br /><br />I skimmed through to the end but have to say - a very poor marriage of historical fiction (hysterical maybe) and Harlequin romance.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H10MbTYDEMYMYAA2p0QfBMTI1ozIPvYF1tbgRZ+y2HUAzlRjNmPfpOLoXAOoYOspLLaXkfXaKgrJc+3XjDaVSQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zTzcpIc0VS7h1skU4c7IEIneAcvWvuSuA+IFRiyCwF3Sr4Sqh1SaTA9elSHu6jw9YaBA1utaOKEcRwjUPwaNYQ==')})
  }

Aos 10 anos já falava inglês, francês e latim. Cursou a faculdade de Direito em São Paulo e teve praticamente toda a sua obra publicada após a sua morte. Como escritor brilhante que foi e poeta original e talentoso, a qualidade da sua obra surpreende pela precocidade com que foi concebida. Discípulo dos românticos europeus, como Byron, Hoffmann e Shelley, seus textos refletem o ambiente de sua época, onde a literatura estava impregnada de pessimismo, ceticismo, morbidez e pressentimento da morte. Este Rimbaud tropical escreveu Noite na taverna, um clássico composto de sete contos ímpares na literatura de língua portuguesa, a genial coletânea de seus poemas, Lira dos 20 Anos, e outros textos como Cartas, a série humorística Spleen e Charutos, Poema do Frade, O Conde Lopo, entre outras obras. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5325253864776165179">Anne Fortier grew up in Denmark, but immigrated to the United States in 2002. She holds a Ph.D. in the History of Ideas and co-produced the Emmy-winning documentary Fire and Ice: The Winter War of Finland and Russia (2005). Her first novel in English, JULIET (2010), was published in over 30 countries and became a New York Times bestseller. Her next book, THE LOST SISTERHOOD (2014), will be out in </span>
  <span id="freeText5325253864776165179" style="display:none">Anne Fortier grew up in Denmark, but immigrated to the United States in 2002. She holds a Ph.D. in the History of Ideas and co-produced the Emmy-winning documentary Fire and Ice: The Winter War of Finland and Russia (2005). Her first novel in English, JULIET (2010), was published in over 30 countries and became a New York Times bestseller. Her next book, THE LOST SISTERHOOD (2014), will be out in paperback on September 1, 2015.</span>
